The Definition of Contradiction: Genus and Differentia
Definition of contradiction with genus and differentia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the proximate genus and differentia from the definition of contradiction and verify its completeness.

Core Idea
Contradiction is difference by negation/affirmation plus the condition of necessary truth disparity.

In this passage, the author defines contradiction as a type of opposition. The definition has a clear genus (difference by negation and affirmation) and a differentia (necessitates that one is true and the other false). Understanding this structure is essential for recognizing when two propositions genuinely contradict each other, which is crucial in Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh) for resolving apparent conflicts between evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find 'contradiction' (التناقض) in the Arabic. The author says it is a type of opposition.
2
Extract the genus
The author says 'difference by negation and affirmation' (الاختلاف بالسلب والإيجاب) is the proximate genus. Note that absolute difference is the remote genus.
3
Extract the differentia
The phrase 'in a manner that necessitates by itself that one of them is true and the other false' is the differentia. This distinguishes contradiction from other differences.
4
Test the definition's completeness
Check if the definition includes all instances of contradiction and excludes non-contradictions. Does it cover essential and non-essential mutual exclusion? The author later discusses divisions, so the definition works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الرابع: في التناقض والعكس وما يتعلّق بهما في الحمليات والشرطيات وفي هذا النوع من المباحث: أما الأول منها فذلك في التناقض؛ قد مرَّ من قبل أن التناقض نوع من التقابل. وإنه أي التناقض عبارة عن اختلاف قضيتين بالسلب والإيجاب على وجه يقتضى لذاته أن تكون إحداهما صادقة والأخرى كاذبة. فالاختلاف بالسلب والإيجاب هو جنسه القريب، والباقي هو فصله. والاختلاف مطلقًا هو الجنس البعيد ينقسم إلى [أ] الاختلاف بينهما بالسلب والإيجاب؛ [ب] وإلى الاختلاف بينهما لا بالسلب والإيجاب. والاختلاف بينهما بالسلب والإيجاب ينقسم [أ] إلى ما يكون بين المتنافيين كما في قولنا هذا الشيء متحرّك، هذا الشيء ليس بمتحرك ؛ [ب] وإلى ما لا يكون بين المتنافيين كما في هذا متحرّك، هذا ليس بساكن. والتنافي أيضًا ينقسم [1] إلى ما يكون بالذات كما في قولنا هذا إنسان هذا ليس بإنسان؛ [ب] وإلى ما لا يكون بالذات كما في قولنا هذا إنسان، هذا ليس بحيوان. فإن التنافي بينهما باعتبار أن يكون الإنسان حيوانا بالضرورة. ثم الصادقة من القضيتين المتناقضتين قد تكون معينة وقد لا تكون؛ وذلك لأن الحكم بالشيء على الشيء لا يخلو من أن يكون في مادة الوجوب أو مادة الامتناع أو في مادة الإمكان على ما عرف فلو كان الحكم بينهما في مادة الوجوب لكانت الصادقة منهما هي الموجبة كما في قولنا كل إنسان حيوان بعض الإنسان ليس بحيوان. وإن كان في مادة الامتناع كانت الصادقة هي السالبة كما في قولنا كل إنسان صهَّال، بعض الإنسان ليس بصهال، وأما الكاذبة فيهما فعلى عكس الموجبة. وإن كان في مادة الإمكان فالصادقة منهما لا تكون متعينة، والكاذبة كذلك إلا في الممكن الماضي والحاضر. فأما في المستقبل كما يقال زيد يمشي غدًا، زيد لا يمشي غدًا، فلا يتعين أحدهما البتة؛ إذ لو تعين
The fourth type: On contradiction and conversion and what pertains to them in categoricals and conditionals. In this type of investigation: as for the first of them, that is on contradiction. It has passed before that contradiction is a type of opposition. And it, i.e., contradiction, is the difference of two propositions by negation and affirmation in a manner that necessitates by itself that one of them is true and the other false. So the difference by negation and affirmation is its proximate genus, and the remainder is its differentia. And absolute difference is the remote genus, dividing into [a] the difference between them by negation and affirmation; [b] and the difference between them not by negation and affirmation. And the difference between them by negation and affirmation divides [a] into what is between mutually exclusive things, as in our saying 'This thing is moving, this thing is not moving'; [b] and into what is not between mutually exclusive things, as in 'This is moving, this is not at rest'. And mutual exclusion also divides [1] into what is essential, as in our saying 'This is a human, this is not a human'; [b] and into what is not essential, as in our saying 'This is a human, this is not an animal'. For the mutual exclusion between them is by virtue that a human is necessarily an animal. Then the true among the two contradictory propositions may be determinate or may not be; and that is because the judgment of a thing about a thing cannot be other than in matter of necessity, or matter of impossibility, or in matter of possibility, as was known. So if the judgment between them is in matter of necessity, then the true among them is the affirmative, as in our saying 'Every human is an animal, some human is not an animal'. And if it is in matter of impossibility, then the true one is the negative, as in our saying 'Every human is a neighing animal, some human is not a neighing animal'. And as for the false in both, it is the opposite of the affirmative. And if it is in matter of possibility, then the true among them is not determinate, and the false likewise, except in the possible past and present. As for the future, as is said 'Zayd will walk tomorrow, Zayd will not walk tomorrow', then neither of them is ever determinate; for if it were determinate...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a definition and division of contradiction (التناقض). The author begins by stating that contradiction is a type of opposition. He defines it precisely: the difference between two propositions by negation and affirmation in a way that necessitates by itself that one is true and the other false. Here, 'difference by negation and affirmation' is the proximate genus, and the condition 'necessitates by itself that one is true and the other false' is the differentia. The author then expands on the genus: absolute difference (الاختلاف مطلقًا) is the remote genus, which divides into difference by negation/affirmation and difference not by negation/affirmation. The former further divides into difference between mutually exclusive terms (like 'moving' vs 'not moving') and difference not between mutually exclusive terms (like 'moving' vs 'not at rest'). Mutual exclusion (التنافي) itself divides into essential (e.g., 'human' vs 'not human') and non-essential (e.g., 'human' vs 'not animal', because 'not animal' excludes 'human' only accidentally due to the necessary relation that human is animal). The author then discusses the truth-values of contradictory propositions based on the 'matter' (مادة) of the judgment: necessity, impossibility, or possibility. In matter of necessity, the affirmative is true (e.g., 'Every human is an animal' vs 'Some human is not an animal'); in impossibility, the negative is true (e.g., 'Every human is a neighing animal' vs 'Some human is not a neighing animal'); in possibility, the truth is indeterminate except for past and present possibilities. For future contingents, like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' vs 'Zayd will not walk tomorrow', neither is determinately true or false. This reflects the Islamic logical doctrine of future contingents, preserving free will and divine knowledge.

Key Terms
التناقض
المادة
المتنافيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proximate genus of contradiction?
A) Absolute difference
B) Difference by negation and affirmation
C) Mutual exclusion
D) Opposition

Key Takeaway
The definition of contradiction combines a genus (difference by negation/affirmation) with a differentia (necessitates truth disparity), making it a precise logical tool.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Divisions of Difference: From Absolute Difference to Contradiction
Division of difference and mutual exclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify differences between propositions using the tree of divisions presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Not every negation/affirmation pair is a contradiction; it must be between mutually exclusive terms.

The author expands on the genus of contradiction by showing how difference (al-ikhtilāf) is divided. Absolute difference splits into difference by negation/affirmation and other differences. The former then splits into difference between mutually exclusive terms (which leads to contradiction) and difference not between mutually exclusive terms (which does not). Understanding this tree helps in identifying genuine contradictions in Islamic scholarly debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main branches of absolute difference
The passage says absolute difference divides into (1) difference by negation/affirmation and (2) difference not by negation/affirmation.
2
Further divide difference by negation/affirmation
It divides into (a) difference between mutually exclusive terms (e.g., moving/not moving) and (b) difference not between mutually exclusive terms (e.g., moving/not at rest). Only (a) leads to contradiction.
3
Distinguish essential vs non-essential mutual exclusion
Mutual exclusion itself divides into essential (human/not human) and non-essential (human/not animal) depending on whether the exclusion is inherent or by virtue of a necessary relation.

Truth in Contradiction: The Role of Matter (Māddah)
Truth conditions based on matter in contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine which contradictory proposition is true based on the matter (necessity, impossibility, possibility) of the judgment.

Core Idea
The truth of contradictory propositions depends not on form alone but on the ontological matter of the subject-predicate relation.

The author explains that the truth among contradictory propositions is not always the same; it depends on the 'matter' (al-māddah) of the judgment, i.e., whether the relation is necessary, impossible, or possible. This is crucial for evaluating theological arguments where the matter is often necessity (e.g., God exists) or impossibility (e.g., God is ignorant).

Guided Path
1
Recall the three types of matter
Necessity (wujūb), impossibility (imtinā'), possibility (imkān). The subject-predicate relation must be one of these.
2
Determine truth in matter of necessity
The affirmative proposition is true, as in 'Every human is an animal'. The negative is false.
3
Determine truth in matter of impossibility
The negative proposition is true, as in 'Every human is a neighing animal' (impossible), so 'Some human is not a neighing animal' is true.
4
Determine truth in matter of possibility
Neither is determinately true, except for past and present possibilities. For future contingents, both are indeterminate.

النوع الرابع: في التناقض والعكس وما يتعلّق بهما في الحمليات والشرطيات وفي هذا النوع من المباحث: أما الأول منها فذلك في التناقض؛ قد مرَّ من قبل أن التناقض نوع من التقابل. وإنه أي التناقض عبارة عن اختلاف قضيتين بالسلب والإيجاب على وجه يقتضى لذاته أن تكون إحداهما صادقة والأخرى كاذبة. فالاختلاف بالسلب والإيجاب هو جنسه القريب، والباقي هو فصله. والاختلاف مطلقًا هو الجنس البعيد ينقسم إلى [أ] الاختلاف بينهما بالسلب والإيجاب؛ [ب] وإلى الاختلاف بينهما لا بالسلب والإيجاب. والاختلاف بينهما بالسلب والإيجاب ينقسم [أ] إلى ما يكون بين المتنافيين كما في قولنا هذا الشيء متحرّك، هذا الشيء ليس بمتحرك ؛ [ب] وإلى ما لا يكون بين المتنافيين كما في هذا متحرّك، هذا ليس بساكن. والتنافي أيضًا ينقسم [1] إلى ما يكون بالذات كما في قولنا هذا إنسان هذا ليس بإنسان؛ [ب] وإلى ما لا يكون بالذات كما في قولنا هذا إنسان، هذا ليس بحيوان. فإن التنافي بينهما باعتبار أن يكون الإنسان حيوانا بالضرورة. ثم الصادقة من القضيتين المتناقضتين قد تكون معينة وقد لا تكون؛ وذلك لأن الحكم بالشيء على الشيء لا يخلو من أن يكون في مادة الوجوب أو مادة الامتناع أو في مادة الإمكان على ما عرف فلو كان الحكم بينهما في مادة الوجوب لكانت الصادقة منهما هي الموجبة كما في قولنا كل إنسان حيوان بعض الإنسان ليس بحيوان. وإن كان في مادة الامتناع كانت الصادقة هي السالبة كما في قولنا كل إنسان صهَّال، بعض الإنسان ليس بصهال، وأما الكاذبة فيهما فعلى عكس الموجبة. وإن كان في مادة الإمكان فالصادقة منهما لا تكون متعينة، والكاذبة كذلك إلا في الممكن الماضي والحاضر. فأما في المستقبل كما يقال زيد يمشي غدًا، زيد لا يمشي غدًا، فلا يتعين أحدهما البتة؛ إذ لو تعين
The fourth type: On contradiction and conversion and what pertains to them in categoricals and conditionals. In this type of investigation: as for the first of them, that is on contradiction. It has passed before that contradiction is a type of opposition. And it, i.e., contradiction, is the difference of two propositions by negation and affirmation in a manner that necessitates by itself that one of them is true and the other false. So the difference by negation and affirmation is its proximate genus, and the remainder is its differentia. And absolute difference is the remote genus, dividing into [a] the difference between them by negation and affirmation; [b] and the difference between them not by negation and affirmation. And the difference between them by negation and affirmation divides [a] into what is between mutually exclusive things, as in our saying 'This thing is moving, this thing is not moving'; [b] and into what is not between mutually exclusive things, as in 'This is moving, this is not at rest'. And mutual exclusion also divides [1] into what is essential, as in our saying 'This is a human, this is not a human'; [b] and into what is not essential, as in our saying 'This is a human, this is not an animal'. For the mutual exclusion between them is by virtue that a human is necessarily an animal. Then the true among the two contradictory propositions may be determinate or may not be; and that is because the judgment of a thing about a thing cannot be other than in matter of necessity, or matter of impossibility, or in matter of possibility, as was known. So if the judgment between them is in matter of necessity, then the true among them is the affirmative, as in our saying 'Every human is an animal, some human is not an animal'. And if it is in matter of impossibility, then the true one is the negative, as in our saying 'Every human is a neighing animal, some human is not a neighing animal'. And as for the false in both, it is the opposite of the affirmative. And if it is in matter of possibility, then the true among them is not determinate, and the false likewise, except in the possible past and present. As for the future, as is said 'Zayd will walk tomorrow, Zayd will not walk tomorrow', then neither of them is ever determinate; for if it were determinate...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a definition and division of contradiction (التناقض). The author begins by stating that contradiction is a type of opposition. He defines it precisely: the difference between two propositions by negation and affirmation in a way that necessitates by itself that one is true and the other false. Here, 'difference by negation and affirmation' is the proximate genus, and the condition 'necessitates by itself that one is true and the other false' is the differentia. The author then expands on the genus: absolute difference (الاختلاف مطلقًا) is the remote genus, which divides into difference by negation/affirmation and difference not by negation/affirmation. The former further divides into difference between mutually exclusive terms (like 'moving' vs 'not moving') and difference not between mutually exclusive terms (like 'moving' vs 'not at rest'). Mutual exclusion (التنافي) itself divides into essential (e.g., 'human' vs 'not human') and non-essential (e.g., 'human' vs 'not animal', because 'not animal' excludes 'human' only accidentally due to the necessary relation that human is animal). The author then discusses the truth-values of contradictory propositions based on the 'matter' (مادة) of the judgment: necessity, impossibility, or possibility. In matter of necessity, the affirmative is true (e.g., 'Every human is an animal' vs 'Some human is not an animal'); in impossibility, the negative is true (e.g., 'Every human is a neighing animal' vs 'Some human is not a neighing animal'); in possibility, the truth is indeterminate except for past and present possibilities. For future contingents, like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' vs 'Zayd will not walk tomorrow', neither is determinately true or false. This reflects the Islamic logical doctrine of future contingents, preserving free will and divine knowledge.

Key Terms
المادة
الوجوب
الامتناع
الإمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in matter of impossibility, which proposition is true?
A) The affirmative
B) The negative
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The truth of a contradictory pair is not symmetrical; it is determined by the ontological matter of the judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
For each contradictory pair, identify the matter and state which proposition is true according to the passage: (1) 'Every intoxicant is haram' vs 'Some intoxicant is not haram'; (2) 'Every human is a stone' vs 'Some human is not a stone'; (3) 'Zayd is writing now' vs 'Zayd is not writing now' (present possibility).

Future Contingents: Why Contradictory Propositions Can Be Indeterminate
Indeterminacy of truth in future contingent contradictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why future contingent propositions do not have a determinate truth value in contradiction, according to Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Future free actions are neither determinately true nor false, preserving human choice and divine omniscience.

The passage concludes with a profound point: in possible matters concerning the future, contradictory propositions like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' and 'Zayd will not walk tomorrow' are neither determinately true nor false. This is not a logical flaw but a deliberate doctrine that upholds free will and the nature of contingent events. This position differs from Aristotelian logic and has important implications for kalam arguments about divine foreknowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception for past and present
The passage says except in possible matters of the past and present, where one may be determinately true. For example, 'Zayd is walking now' vs 'Zayd is not walking now' has a determinate truth (the one matching reality).
2
Understand the future case
For future possibilities, the matter is the same (possibility), but the event has not occurred yet. So neither proposition is determinately true at present.
3
Connect to the definition of contradiction
The definition says that contradiction necessitates that one is true and the other false. For future contingents, this holds in the sense that eventually one will become true when the future becomes present, but currently they are indeterminate. The passage seems to imply that the necessity in the definition is about the logical relation (it necessitates that one must be true and the other false) but in future contingents, the determinacy is suspended because the matter is not yet actualized.

Contradictory of Absolute Propositions: The Permanence Qualifier
Author rejects common view and introduces permanence qualifier for absolute contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why an absolute proposition cannot be contradicted by another absolute proposition, and construct the correct contradictory using a permanence qualifier.

Core Idea
Absolute propositions require a permanence qualifier in their contradictory to avoid temporal ambiguity.

In this passage, the author challenges the common assumption that the contradictory of an absolute proposition is simply its opposite in quantity and quality. He demonstrates that because absolute propositions are temporally unrestricted, two such propositions can be true at different times, thus not contradicting each other. The only way to guarantee contradiction is to include a qualifier of permanence (dawām) in the contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absolute proposition
An absolute proposition like 'Every B is C' lacks any temporal or modal qualifier. Recognise that its truth is not tied to a specific time.
2
Recognise the problem with the simple contradictory
The simple contradictory 'Some B is not C' can be true at a different time than the original. If the original is true at one time and false at another, the simple contradictory can also be true at that other time, so both can be false at the same time? Actually, the point is that they can both be false only if the original is not permanent and the contradictory holds at a different time. The author says: 'it is possible that it is not permanent; if it were so, this [the absolute] would not be opposed to that [the particular negative] because of the possibility that this is in one time and that in another.'
Contradiction requires that the two propositions cannot both be true and cannot both be false under the same conditions.
3
Add the permanence qualifier
The author concludes that the contradictory must include a qualifier of permanence, specifically a permanent negation, to ensure that the original and its contradictory cannot both be true at any time. 'Permanent negation contradicts both permanent and non-permanent affirmation.'
4
Form the correct contradictory
For 'Every B is C (absolutely)', the correct contradictory is 'Some B is not C permanently'. The permanence qualifier indicates that the negation holds at all times, ensuring true contradiction.
The permanence qualifier is not itself the contradictory but is necessary to indicate it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: [ في التناقض في الحمليات ] ولما كانت القضية منقسمة إلى الأقسام التي مرَّ ذكرها في الجهات ويتعين كل قسم من تلك الأقسام في الحمليّات والشرطيات فلا بد من أن يتعين نقيض كل قسم من الأقسام ويتبين بأنه نقيضه. والنقيض للواحد منها واحد ليس إلا ؛ إذ المحمول الواحد من موضوع واحد في زمان واحد بجهة واحدة لا يمكن أن يسلب عنه مرة بعد مرة بل مرة واحدة كما في الإيجاب. والزمان من جملة ما يجب رعاية اتحاده بالحقيقة في المطلقات والموجهات. والرعاية أمر صعب لا يمكن كل واحد في كل صورة بل لا يمكن أصلا في البعض من الصور، فالمنطقي يضطر إلى التنبيه على نقيض كل واحدة من القضايا المطلقة والموجهة . والمشهور في المطلقة أن لها نقيضا من جنسها لكنه لا يكون كذلك. فإنا إذا قلنا كل «ب ج» مثلا ولا نتعرض لهذا الحمل أن يكون بالضرورة، أو لا بالضرورة، أو بالدوام، أو لا بالدوام البتة، فلا يناقض هذا القول قولنا بعض «ب» ليس «ب» «ج» على الإطلاق. فإن من المحتمل أن لا يكون دائمًا فبتقدير أن يكون كذلك لا يكون هذا منافيًا لذلك الاحتمال أن يكون هذا في وقت وذلك في وقت آخر بل لا بد من اعتبار قيد الدوام في النقيض؛ إذ السلب الدائم ينافي الإيجاب الدائم وغير الدائم. ثم الدوام قد يكون ضروريا، وقد لا يكون لكنه لا يمكن أن يكون مقيدا بأحد هذين القيدين في هذه الصورة لصحة اجتماع المطلقة مع كل واحد منهما على الكذب عندما يكون الصادق القسم الآخر فيلزم أن يعتبر قيد الدوام عند الإطلاق لا على معنى أن هذه الدائمة نفس النقيض بل على معنى أنه لا يمكن الإشارة إلى النقيض إلا به؛ فيقال كل «أب» بالإطلاق، بعض ( أ ) ليس «ب» دائمًا. وكما أن المطلقة لا يناقضها من نوعها شيء البتة فكذلك الغير أي قضية كانت من القضايا الموجّهة فلا يناقضها من نوعها شيء لصحة اجتماعها على الكذب عندما يكون الصادق هو المخالف في الجهة بل الذي يناقضها ما يخالف في الكم والكيف والجهة جميعا؛ فنقيض قولنا بالضرورة كل «أب» ليس بالضرورة كل «أب»، وهذا هو سلب الضرورة التي مرَّ ذكرها. وسلب الضرورة غير ضرورة السلب. وكذلك سلب الدوام غیر دوام السلب، وسلب الإمكان غير إمكان السلب؛ غير أنه وهو النقيض قد يمكن أن يعبر بعبارة لا يفهم منها إلا ما هو النقيض بعينه، وقد لا يمكن كما مرّ من قبل. فيعبر إذن بما يدل عليه من العبارات، وإن لم يدل عليه صريحًا فيقال نقيض الضرورة المطلقة، الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا لما أن للشيء إما أن يكون ضروري الوجود، أو ضروري العدم، أو لا ضروري الوجود
Section: On Contradiction in Categorical Propositions. Since the proposition is divided into the divisions mentioned in the modalities, and each division of those divisions is specified in categoricals and conditionals, it is necessary that the contradictory of each division be specified and made clear that it is its contradictory. And the contradictory of one [proposition] is only one; for the same predicate from the same subject in the same time and from the same aspect cannot be negated again and again, but only once, as in affirmation. Time is among the things that must be considered as identical in reality in absolute and modal propositions. And its consideration is a difficult matter; not everyone can [do it] in every case, indeed it is impossible in some cases. So the logician is forced to point out the contradictory of each absolute and modal proposition. It is well-known that the absolute [proposition] has a contradictory of its own kind, but it is not so. For if we say 'Every B is C' for example, and we do not attend to whether this predication is necessary, or not necessary, or permanent, or not permanent at all, then this statement is not contradicted by our statement 'Some B is not C' absolutely. For it is possible that it is not permanent; if it were so, this [the absolute] would not be opposed to that [the particular negative] because of the possibility that this is in one time and that in another. Rather, the qualifier of permanence must be considered in the contradictory; for permanent negation contradicts both permanent and non-permanent affirmation. Then permanence may be necessary, and it may not be, but it cannot be qualified by either of these two qualifiers in this case, because the absolute can be true together with each of them when the true is the other kind; so it is necessary to consider the qualifier of permanence in the absolute, not meaning that this permanent is itself the contradictory, but meaning that the contradictory cannot be indicated except by it. So it is said: 'Every A is B absolutely' [and] 'Some A is not B permanently'. And just as the absolute is not contradicted by anything of its own kind at all, so too any other modal proposition is not contradicted by anything of its own kind, because they can be together false when the true is the one that differs in modality. Rather, what contradicts it is what differs in quantity, quality, and modality altogether. So the contradictory of our statement 'Necessarily, every A is B' is 'Not necessarily, every A is B', and this is the negation of necessity previously mentioned. And the negation of necessity is not the necessity of negation. Similarly, the negation of permanence is not the permanence of negation, and the negation of possibility is not the possibility of negation. However, the contradictory can sometimes be expressed by an expression from which only the contradictory itself is understood, and sometimes it cannot, as previously mentioned. So one expresses it by expressions that indicate it, even if not explicitly. So it is said: 'The contradictory of absolute necessity is the general possible that differs in quantity and quality, because a thing is either necessary of existence, or necessary of non-existence, or not necessary of existence.'
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage explains how to determine the contradictory (naqīḍ) of categorical propositions, especially absolute (muṭlaqa) and modal (muwajjaha) ones. The author begins by stating that since propositions are divided into types based on modality, each type requires a unique contradictory. This is because the contradictory of a single proposition must be unique: the same predicate cannot be affirmed and denied of the same subject under the same conditions. Time is a critical element that must be identical, but its verification is difficult, so the logician must explicitly specify the contradictory. The common view that an absolute proposition has a contradictory of the same kind (i.e., another absolute) is rejected. For example, 'Every B is C' without temporal specification is not contradicted by 'Some B is not C' absolutely, because the absolute could be true at one time and the particular negative at another. Instead, the contradictory must include a qualifier of permanence (dawām); thus the contradictory of an absolute universal affirmative is a particular negative with permanent negation: 'Some A is not B permanently'. This permanence may be necessary or not, but it is not itself the contradictory; it is a necessary indicator. The same principle applies to modal propositions: they are not contradicted by another modal of the same kind, because they can both be false when the truth is of a different modality. The contradictory must differ in quantity (kamm), quality (kayf), and modality (jiha). For instance, the contradictory of 'Necessarily, every A is B' is 'Not necessarily, every A is B'—i.e., the negation of necessity, not the necessity of negation. The author clarifies that the negation of necessity is not the necessity of negation, and similarly for permanence and possibility. Sometimes the contradictory can be expressed directly, sometimes not; in the latter case, one uses a phrase that indicates the contradictory, such as 'the contradictory of absolute necessity is the general possible that differs in quantity and quality'.

Contradictory of Modal Propositions: Changing Quantity, Quality, and Modality
Author gives rule for modal contradictory and distinguishes negation of modality from modality of negation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory of a modal categorical proposition by changing quantity, quality, and modality.

Core Idea
Modal propositions are contradicted only by propositions that differ in quantity, quality, and modality.

The author extends the principle to modal propositions: no modal proposition has a contradictory of the same modal kind. Instead, the contradictory must differ in all three respects: quantity (universal/particular), quality (affirmative/negative), and modality (necessity/permanence/possibility). He illustrates with the example of necessary universal affirmative, whose contradictory is the negation of necessity, not the necessity of negation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modal proposition
Consider a modal proposition like 'Necessarily, every A is B'. Note its quantity (universal), quality (affirmative), and modality (necessity).
2
Recall the rule
The contradictory must differ in quantity, quality, and modality. No proposition of the same modal kind can serve as contradictory because two modals of the same kind can both be false when the true proposition has a different modality.
The author says: 'they can be together false when the true is the one that differs in modality.'
3
Change quantity and quality
If the original is universal affirmative, the contradictory must be particular negative. This changes both quantity and quality.
4
Change modality
The modal operator must be negated, not the predicate. For 'Necessarily, every A is B', the contradictory becomes 'Not necessarily, every A is B' (which is equivalent to a particular negative possible). This is the negation of necessity, not the necessity of negation.
The author emphasizes: 'the negation of necessity is not the necessity of negation.'
5
Distinguish from other forms
Similarly, for permanence and possibility, the negation must be on the modality itself, not on the predicate. If the contradictory cannot be expressed directly, one uses descriptive phrases that indicate the contradictory.

Section: On Contradiction in Categorical Propositions. Since the proposition is divided into the divisions mentioned in the modalities, and each division of those divisions is specified in categoricals and conditionals, it is necessary that the contradictory of each division be specified and made clear that it is its contradictory. And the contradictory of one [proposition] is only one; for the same predicate from the same subject in the same time and from the same aspect cannot be negated again and again, but only once, as in affirmation. Time is among the things that must be considered as identical in reality in absolute and modal propositions. And its consideration is a difficult matter; not everyone can [do it] in every case, indeed it is impossible in some cases. So the logician is forced to point out the contradictory of each absolute and modal proposition. It is well-known that the absolute [proposition] has a contradictory of its own kind, but it is not so. For if we say 'Every B is C' for example, and we do not attend to whether this predication is necessary, or not necessary, or permanent, or not permanent at all, then this statement is not contradicted by our statement 'Some B is not C' absolutely. For it is possible that it is not permanent; if it were so, this [the absolute] would not be opposed to that [the particular negative] because of the possibility that this is in one time and that in another. Rather, the qualifier of permanence must be considered in the contradictory; for permanent negation contradicts both permanent and non-permanent affirmation. Then permanence may be necessary, and it may not be, but it cannot be qualified by either of these two qualifiers in this case, because the absolute can be true together with each of them when the true is the other kind; so it is necessary to consider the qualifier of permanence in the absolute, not meaning that this permanent is itself the contradictory, but meaning that the contradictory cannot be indicated except by it. So it is said: 'Every A is B absolutely' [and] 'Some A is not B permanently'. And just as the absolute is not contradicted by anything of its own kind at all, so too any other modal proposition is not contradicted by anything of its own kind, because they can be together false when the true is the one that differs in modality. Rather, what contradicts it is what differs in quantity, quality, and modality altogether. So the contradictory of our statement 'Necessarily, every A is B' is 'Not necessarily, every A is B', and this is the negation of necessity previously mentioned. And the negation of necessity is not the necessity of negation. Similarly, the negation of permanence is not the permanence of negation, and the negation of possibility is not the possibility of negation. However, the contradictory can sometimes be expressed by an expression from which only the contradictory itself is understood, and sometimes it cannot, as previously mentioned. So one expresses it by expressions that indicate it, even if not explicitly. So it is said: 'The contradictory of absolute necessity is the general possible that differs in quantity and quality, because a thing is either necessary of existence, or necessary of non-existence, or not necessary of existence.'
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage explains how to determine the contradictory (naqīḍ) of categorical propositions, especially absolute (muṭlaqa) and modal (muwajjaha) ones. The author begins by stating that since propositions are divided into types based on modality, each type requires a unique contradictory. This is because the contradictory of a single proposition must be unique: the same predicate cannot be affirmed and denied of the same subject under the same conditions. Time is a critical element that must be identical, but its verification is difficult, so the logician must explicitly specify the contradictory. The common view that an absolute proposition has a contradictory of the same kind (i.e., another absolute) is rejected. For example, 'Every B is C' without temporal specification is not contradicted by 'Some B is not C' absolutely, because the absolute could be true at one time and the particular negative at another. Instead, the contradictory must include a qualifier of permanence (dawām); thus the contradictory of an absolute universal affirmative is a particular negative with permanent negation: 'Some A is not B permanently'. This permanence may be necessary or not, but it is not itself the contradictory; it is a necessary indicator. The same principle applies to modal propositions: they are not contradicted by another modal of the same kind, because they can both be false when the truth is of a different modality. The contradictory must differ in quantity (kamm), quality (kayf), and modality (jiha). For instance, the contradictory of 'Necessarily, every A is B' is 'Not necessarily, every A is B'—i.e., the negation of necessity, not the necessity of negation. The author clarifies that the negation of necessity is not the necessity of negation, and similarly for permanence and possibility. Sometimes the contradictory can be expressed directly, sometimes not; in the latter case, one uses a phrase that indicates the contradictory, such as 'the contradictory of absolute necessity is the general possible that differs in quantity and quality'.

الضرورة
السلب
الجهة

The Contradictory of Absolute Necessary Propositions
Author defines the contradictory of absolute necessary propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proper contradictory of an absolute necessary proposition as a general possibility proposition that differs in quantity and quality.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a necessary proposition is not a negation of necessity but a general possibility.

In this passage, the author explains how to find the contradictory (naqid) of a proposition that affirms something with absolute necessity. The key is to realize that the contradictory must differ both in modality and in quantity/quality. The author argues that the only candidate that satisfies this is the general possibility proposition (al-mumkina al-'amma). We will work through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
The proposition in question is an absolute necessary proposition (al-daruriyya al-mutlaqa), e.g., 'Necessarily every A is B.' Determine its modality and quantity.
Absolute necessity means the predicate holds for all instances of the subject necessarily, without temporal qualification.
2
Determine the criteria for a contradictory
A contradictory must always differ in truth value. For modal propositions, it must also differ in modality or quantity/quality such that they cannot both be true or both false.
The contradictory must be opposite in both truth and modality.
3
Test candidate contradictories
Consider propositions of the same type (e.g., another necessary proposition) and show they can be simultaneously false. This eliminates them.
For example, 'Necessarily every A is B' and 'Necessarily some A is not B' can both be false when the truth is 'Every A is B by special possibility'.
4
Identify the correct contradictory
The general possibility (al-imkan al-'amm) proposition: 'Some A is not B by general possibility.' This differs in quantity (some vs. every) and quality (negative) and modality (possible not vs. necessary). Verify that it always has opposite truth value.
General possibility means 'neither necessary nor impossible'. It negates both necessity and impossibility.
5
Apply the rule
Given any absolute necessary proposition, its contradictory is the corresponding general possibility proposition with opposite quantity and quality.
Example: 'Necessarily every khamr is haram' contradicts 'Some khamr is not haram by general possibility'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإن قيل هب أنه كذلك لكن القضية الموجهة أي قضية كانت ضرورية أو لا ضرورية فهي مشتملة على نفس ثبوت الشيء للشيء، وكيفية ذلك الثبوت فتكون مقيدة إما بقيدين أو ثلاثة قيود مثلا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون النقيض رفع قيد من تلك القيود لا على التعيين. وما ذكرتم لا يكون كذلك فيما ذكرتم وهو الضرورة المطلقة. فنقول قد مرّ من قبل أن النقيض قد يعبر بعبارة يدل عليه وإن لم يدل عليه صريحًا. فالذي مرَّ ذكره إما أن يدل عليه صريحًا؛ وإنه من جملة ما لا كلام فيه، وإما أن لا يدل عليه صريحًا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يدل عليه وإن لم يدل عليه صريحًا وإلا لا يقوم مقام النقيض وهو رفع قيد من القيود التي ذكرتم، والذي مرَّ ذكره وهو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا فإنه يدل عليه. وذلك لأن الإمكان العام هو سلب الضرورة عن جانبها المخالف؛ وهو سلب ضرورة ثبوت الشيء للشيء فيما نحن فيه. وسلب ضرورة ثبوت الشيء للشيء قد يكون برفع الثبوت، وقد يكون برفع الضرورة فيكون دالا على الرفع الذي يلزم ذلك الرفع. وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يناقضها من نوعها شيء فذلك ظاهر لما أمكن اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق قولنا كل «أب» بالإمكان الخاص. وكما أنه لا يمكن أن يناقضها من نوعها شيء فكذلك لا يمكن أن يناقضها غيرها سوى الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا. والعلم بذلك يفتقر إلى أن ينظر في كل قضية من القضايا الموجهة بعينها فإنه يظهر بالنظر فيها أنها من جملة ما لا يمكن أن يناقضها. وكيف يمكن وقد صح اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق هو المخالف لهما في الجهة؛ وهذا هو الحكم الشامل لكل قضية من القضايا الموجهة. فما يوهم أن يناقضها سوى الممكنة العامة هو المطلقة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا لما أنها في مقابلة الدائمة. والدائمة من لوازم الضرورة المطلقة لكنه لا يكون كذلك [١٢٥ظ] فإنه يمكن اجتماعها على الكذب / حال ما يكون الصادق قولنا كل «أب» دائمًا من غير ضرورة.

And the common between them is general possibility, so it is said: necessarily every A is B; some A is not B by general possibility. And what you mentioned is not like that in what you mentioned, namely absolute necessity. So we say: it has passed before that the contradictory may be expressed by a phrase that indicates it even if it does not indicate it explicitly. And what was mentioned, namely the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality, indicates it. That is because general possibility is the negation of necessity from the opposite side; it is the negation of the necessity of a thing's being affirmed of a thing in our case. And the negation of the necessity of a thing's being affirmed of a thing may be by removing the affirmation, or by removing the necessity, so it indicates the removal that entails that removal. And as for the fact that nothing of its own type can contradict it, that is evident because they can both be false when the true statement is 'every A is B' by special possibility. And just as nothing of its own type can contradict it, likewise nothing other than it can contradict it except the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality. And knowledge of that requires examining each modal proposition in itself, for it becomes clear upon examination that it is of those that cannot be contradicted. And how can it be, when they can both be false while the true one is the one that differs from them in modality? And this is the comprehensive judgment for every modal proposition. So what might give the illusion that something other than the general possibility contradicts it is the absolute general that differs in quantity and quality, because it is opposite to the perpetual. And the perpetual is one of the concomitants of absolute necessity, but it is not so, for they can both be false when the true statement is 'every A is B' perpetually without necessity.

Commentary
This passage defines the proper contradictory (naqid) of absolute necessary propositions (al-daruriyya al-mutlaqa). The author begins by explaining that if both necessary existence and necessary non-existence were true, then one cannot be removed without the other remaining, or both become non-necessary, which is special possibility (al-imkan al-khass). The common factor between necessary existence and necessary non-existence is general possibility (al-imkan al-'amm), so the contradictory of a necessary universal affirmative 'necessarily every A is B' is 'some A is not B by general possibility.' The author then addresses an objection: modal propositions consist of both an assertion and a modality, so their contradictory should remove a specific restriction (like the modality or the quantity) without specification. The response is that the contradictory may be expressed indirectly; the general possibility does indicate removal of the necessity condition because it negates the necessity from the opposite side. Furthermore, the author argues that no proposition of the same type can contradict a necessary proposition because they can both be false when the true proposition is a special possibility. Only the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality serves as the proper contradictory. This is demonstrated by considering cases where both the original and the proposed contradictory are false. The passage concludes by refuting a potential misconception that the contradictory is the absolute general (al-mutlaqa al-'amma), which is opposite to the perpetual (al-da'ima), but it is not, as they too can be false together.

Why Other Propositions Fail as Contradictories for Absolute Necessity
Author defends the unique status of general possibility as the contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the argument that no proposition of the same type can contradict an absolute necessary proposition, and explain why the general possibility is the unique contradictory.

Core Idea
Only the general possibility can be the contradictory because it alone cannot be false simultaneously with the necessary proposition.

The author anticipates an objection and provides a deeper justification for why the general possibility is the unique contradictory. He shows that other candidates, including propositions of the same modality and the absolute general proposition, can both be false with the original necessary proposition. Only the general possibility passes the test of always having opposite truth value.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector claims that a modal proposition's contradictory must remove one of its restrictions (modality, quantity, etc.) without specification. Why does the author's solution not meet this on the surface?
The objector expects an explicit removal of a specific restriction.
2
Examine the author's reply
The author distinguishes between explicit and implicit indication. The general possibility implicitly removes the necessity restriction because it negates necessity from the opposite side, which necessarily involves removal of the necessity condition.
The negation of necessity (salb al-darura) inherently indicates removal of the modality.
3
Test same-type propositions
Show that a necessary proposition of the same type (e.g., another necessity) can be false together with the original when the true proposition is a special possibility. Therefore, they cannot be contradictories.
Example: Both 'Necessarily every A is B' and 'Necessarily some A is not B' are false when the truth is 'Every A is B by special possibility'.
4
Test other candidates
Consider the absolute general proposition (al-mutlaqa al-'amma) and show it too can be false with the original. Thus only the general possibility works.
The absolute general proposition 'Every A is B' (without modality) can be false simultaneously with 'Necessarily every A is B' when the truth is 'Every A is B perpetually without necessity'.
5
Formulate the conclusion
The key test for a contradictory is the impossibility of joint falsehood. The general possibility uniquely passes this test for absolute necessary propositions.
The author states that 'nothing of its own type can contradict it' because they can both be false.

ولا ضروري العدم أيضًا. ولو كان كذلك فلا يرتفع إحدى الضرورتين إلا وأن تبقى الضرورة الأخرى، أو اللا ضرورة من الجانبين وهو الإمكان الخاص. والمشترك بينهما هو الإمكان العام فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب»؛ بعض «أ» ليس (ب) بالإمكان العام. ولا يقال إنه لا يمكن أن يكون مشتركا؛ وقد كان واحد من الأقسام الثلاثة هو الامتناع فإنه هو المشترك بينهما باعتبار ضرورة العدم. وضرورة العدم هي الامتناع لكنها مستلزمة لامتناع الوجود كما أن ضرورة الوجود مستلزمة لامتناع العدم. وعلى هذا في كل ما يكون من قبيل الضرورة المطلقة.
وإن قيل هب أنه كذلك لكن القضية الموجهة أي قضية كانت ضرورية أو لا ضرورية فهي مشتملة على نفس ثبوت الشيء للشيء، وكيفية ذلك الثبوت فتكون مقيدة إما بقيدين أو ثلاثة قيود مثلا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون النقيض رفع قيد من تلك القيود لا على التعيين. وما ذكرتم لا يكون كذلك فيما ذكرتم وهو الضرورة المطلقة. فنقول قد مرّ من قبل أن النقيض قد يعبر بعبارة يدل عليه وإن لم يدل عليه صريحًا. فالذي مرَّ ذكره إما أن يدل عليه صريحًا؛ وإنه من جملة ما لا كلام فيه، وإما أن لا يدل عليه صريحًا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يدل عليه وإن لم يدل عليه صريحًا وإلا لا يقوم مقام النقيض وهو رفع قيد من القيود التي ذكرتم، والذي مرَّ ذكره وهو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا فإنه يدل عليه. وذلك لأن الإمكان العام هو سلب الضرورة عن جانبها المخالف؛ وهو سلب ضرورة ثبوت الشيء للشيء فيما نحن فيه. وسلب ضرورة ثبوت الشيء للشيء قد يكون برفع الثبوت، وقد يكون برفع الضرورة فيكون دالا على الرفع الذي يلزم ذلك الرفع. وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يناقضها من نوعها شيء فذلك ظاهر لما أمكن اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق قولنا كل «أب» بالإمكان الخاص. وكما أنه لا يمكن أن يناقضها من نوعها شيء فكذلك لا يمكن أن يناقضها غيرها سوى الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا. والعلم بذلك يفتقر إلى أن ينظر في كل قضية من القضايا الموجهة بعينها فإنه يظهر بالنظر فيها أنها من جملة ما لا يمكن أن يناقضها. وكيف يمكن وقد صح اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق هو المخالف لهما في الجهة؛ وهذا هو الحكم الشامل لكل قضية من القضايا الموجهة. فما يوهم أن يناقضها سوى الممكنة العامة هو المطلقة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا لما أنها في مقابلة الدائمة. والدائمة من لوازم الضرورة المطلقة لكنه لا يكون كذلك [١٢٥ظ] فإنه يمكن اجتماعها على الكذب / حال ما يكون الصادق قولنا كل «أب» دائمًا من غير ضرورة.
And also not necessary non-existence. And if it were so, then one of the two necessities would not be removed unless the other necessity remains, or no necessity from both sides, which is special possibility. And the common between them is general possibility, so it is said: necessarily every A is B; some A is not B by general possibility. And it is not said that it cannot be common; and one of the three divisions is impossibility, for it is the common between them by way of necessary non-existence. And necessary non-existence is impossibility, but it entails impossibility of existence just as necessary existence entails impossibility of non-existence. And upon this in everything that is of the kind of absolute necessity.
And if it is said: suppose it is so, but a modal proposition, whether necessary or not, includes the very affirmation of a thing of a thing and the modality of that affirmation, so it is restricted by either two or three restrictions for example; and then the contradictory must remove one of those restrictions without specification. And what you mentioned is not like that in what you mentioned, namely absolute necessity. So we say: it has passed before that the contradictory may be expressed by a phrase that indicates it even if it does not indicate it explicitly. So what was mentioned either indicates it explicitly—and it is something about which there is no dispute—or it does not indicate it explicitly; and then it must indicate it even if it does not indicate it explicitly, otherwise it does not serve as the contradictory which is the removal of a restriction from the restrictions you mentioned. And what was mentioned, namely the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality, indicates it. That is because general possibility is the negation of necessity from the opposite side; it is the negation of the necessity of a thing's being affirmed of a thing in our case. And the negation of the necessity of a thing's being affirmed of a thing may be by removing the affirmation, or by removing the necessity, so it indicates the removal that entails that removal. And as for the fact that nothing of its own type can contradict it, that is evident because they can both be false when the true statement is 'every A is B' by special possibility. And just as nothing of its own type can contradict it, likewise nothing other than it can contradict it except the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality. And knowledge of that requires examining each modal proposition in itself, for it becomes clear upon examination that it is of those that cannot be contradicted. And how can it be, when they can both be false while the true one is the one that differs from them in modality? And this is the comprehensive judgment for every modal proposition. So what might give the illusion that something other than the general possibility contradicts it is the absolute general that differs in quantity and quality, because it is opposite to the perpetual. And the perpetual is one of the concomitants of absolute necessity, but it is not so, for they can both be false when the true statement is 'every A is B' perpetually without necessity.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage defines the proper contradictory (naqid) of absolute necessary propositions (al-daruriyya al-mutlaqa). The author begins by explaining that if both necessary existence and necessary non-existence were true, then one cannot be removed without the other remaining, or both become non-necessary, which is special possibility (al-imkan al-khass). The common factor between necessary existence and necessary non-existence is general possibility (al-imkan al-'amm), so the contradictory of a necessary universal affirmative 'necessarily every A is B' is 'some A is not B by general possibility.' The author then addresses an objection: modal propositions consist of both an assertion and a modality, so their contradictory should remove a specific restriction (like the modality or the quantity) without specification. The response is that the contradictory may be expressed indirectly; the general possibility does indicate removal of the necessity condition because it negates the necessity from the opposite side. Furthermore, the author argues that no proposition of the same type can contradict a necessary proposition because they can both be false when the true proposition is a special possibility. Only the general possibility that differs in quantity and quality serves as the proper contradictory. This is demonstrated by considering cases where both the original and the proposed contradictory are false. The passage concludes by refuting a potential misconception that the contradictory is the absolute general (al-mutlaqa al-'amma), which is opposite to the perpetual (al-da'ima), but it is not, as they too can be false together.

الإمكان العام
الإمكان الخاص

الدائمة

Contradictory of the General Conditional (Subject Side)
Author identifies the contradictory for general conditional propositions from the subject side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the contradictory of any general conditional proposition from the subject side by applying the rule of removing one restriction while changing quantity and quality.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conditional necessity must shift in quantity, quality, and modality.

In modal logic, contradicting a conditional proposition is not as simple as negating the necessity. The author demonstrates that the proper contradictory of a general conditional from the subject side involves a precise transformation: it must remove one of three restrictions and simultaneously alter both quantity and quality. This lesson unpacks that rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three restrictions
In the original proposition 'necessarily every A is B as long as it is A', note the three restrictions: necessity (al-darura), the condition (as long as it is A), and universal quantity (kulli). These must be considered to find the contradictory.
2
Recognize the need to remove one restriction
The contradictory must negate the entire proposition. Since the proposition has multiple restricting factors, the contradictory removes one of them. Which one is removed here? It removes the necessity while keeping the condition.
The author specifies that the contradictory removes a restriction from the three.
3
Change quantity and quality
The contradictory changes universal quantity to particular (from 'every' to 'some') and changes affirmative quality to negative (from 'is' to 'is not'). This is required to properly oppose the original.
4
Adjust modality
The modality shifts from necessity (bi al-darura) to general possibility (bi al-imkan al-'amm). This is the removal of the necessity restriction.
General possibility here means 'some A is not B when it is A' is possible, not necessary.
5
Verify with the example
The original is 'necessarily every A is B as long as it is A'. The contradictory given is 'some A is not B when it is A by general possibility'. Check that it differs in quantity, quality, and modality while keeping the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣] وأما في المشروطة العامة من جانب الموضوع فالذي يدل على رفع قيد من القيود الثلاثة فيها هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» ما دام «أ»، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «أب» الإمكان العام.
[3] And as for the general conditional from the subject side, that which indicates the removal of a restriction from the three restrictions in it is the general possibility conditional that differs in quantity and quality, so it is said: necessarily every A is B as long as it is A, some A is not B when it is A by general possibility.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage specifies the contradictory (naqid) for a general conditional proposition from the side of the subject (al-mashruta al-'amma min janib al-mawdu'). Such a proposition has three restrictions: the necessity, the condition (as long as it is A), and the universal quantity. The proper contradictory must remove one of these restrictions. The author identifies that the proposition that does this is the general possibility conditional (al-mumkina al-'amma al-hiniyya) which differs in both quantity (from universal to particular) and quality (from affirmative to negative). The example given is: the original is 'necessarily every A is B as long as it is A'; its contradictory is 'some A is not B when it is A' with the modality of general possibility. This illustrates how the contradictory negates the necessity while maintaining the temporal condition, but changes the quantity and quality.

Contradictory of the Special Conditional Proposition
Author explains the contradictory for special conditional propositions with four restrictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two candidates for the contradictory of a special conditional proposition and explain why neither is uniquely fixed.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a special conditional is ambiguous between two options.

We now turn to the special conditional, which adds a non-permanence restriction. Unlike the general conditional, its contradictory is not uniquely determined. This lesson dissects the four restrictions and the two candidate contradictories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four restrictions
The special conditional has four restrictions: necessity (al-darura), condition (being A), universality (kulliyya), and non-permanence (al-la dawam). The first three are also in the general conditional; the fourth is unique.
2
Understand the non-permanence restriction
Non-permanence means the judgment does not hold at all times, but only under the condition of being A. For example, 'necessarily every A is B not perpetually' means the necessity is only when the subject is A, and not always.
This distinguishes it from perpetual propositions.
3
Recognize the two candidate contradictories
The two candidates are: (1) the general possibility conditional that differs in quantity and quality (e.g., 'some A is not B when it is A by general possibility'), and (2) the perpetual proposition that agrees in quality (e.g., 'some A is perpetually').
These are the only ways to remove one of the four restrictions.
4
See why neither candidate is exact
The first candidate can be false when the original statement 'necessarily every A is B not perpetually' is true, but also when the original is false? Actually, the passage says both candidates can be false together with certain true statements: for the first, when 'necessarily every A is B' is true; for the second, when 'necessarily no A is B' is true. So neither is the perfect contradictory.
Thus, the contradictory is not uniquely determined.
5
Conclude the ambiguity
The author states that neither is the exact contradictory; rather, one of them without specification (la 'ala al-ta'yin) serves as the contradictory. This means in practice we must consider context or accept ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤] وأما المشروطة الخاصة ففيها من القيود ما ليس في العامة وهو قيد اللا دوام فالذي يدل على رفع قيد من تلك القيود الأربعة هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل أ (ب) لا دائمًا، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «أب» الإمكان العام أو بعضه «أ» دائمًا. فلا هذا هو النقيض لعينه ولا ذلك كذلك بل أحدهما لا على التعيين؛ إما هذا فلأنه يمكن اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يصدق قولنا بالضرورة كل «أب». وإما ذلك فلأنه يمكن اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يصدق قولنا بالضرورة لا شيء من «أب».
[4] And as for the special conditional, in it there are restrictions not present in the general one, namely the restriction of non-permanence, so that which indicates the removal of a restriction from those four restrictions is either the general possibility conditional that differs in quantity and quality, or the perpetual that agrees in quality. So it is said: necessarily every A is B not perpetually, some A is not B when it is A by general possibility, or some A is perpetually. So neither this is the exact contradictory nor that, rather one of them without specification. Either this because they can both be false when the statement 'necessarily every A is B' is true. Or that because they can both be false when the statement 'necessarily nothing is A is B' is true.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage addresses the contradictory for special conditional propositions (al-mashruta al-khassa), which have an additional restriction of non-permanence (al-la dawam) beyond the three in the general conditional. The four restrictions are: necessity, condition (as long as it is A), universality, and non-permanence. The author explains that there are two candidates for the contradictory: (1) the general possibility conditional that differs in quantity and quality (similar to the previous case), and (2) the perpetual proposition (al-da'ima) that agrees in quality (e.g., if original is affirmative, the perpetual is also affirmative but with different quantity). The examples given: the original is 'necessarily every A is B not perpetually' (meaning necessarily but not always). The first candidate is 'some A is not B when it is A by general possibility'; the second is 'some A is perpetually (i.e., always).' The author notes that neither is the exact contradictory; rather, either one can serve as the contradictory without specification. This is because both can be false together with certain true statements: the first candidate is false when the original is true, but could also be false when the original is false? The text explains that they can both be false when 'necessarily every A is B' is true, meaning that if the original is a special conditional with non-permanence, the general possibility conditional can be false at the same time as another proposition. Similarly, the perpetual can be false when 'necessarily nothing is A is B' is true. Thus, the contradictory is not uniquely determined.

اللا دوام

The Contradictory of Modal Propositions
Author states the general principle for contradictories of modal propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory of any modal proposition in Islamic logic and distinguish it from other modal forms.

Core Idea
The only true contradictory of a modal proposition is the general possible opposite in quantity and quality.

In modal logic, finding the contradictory of a quantified modal statement is not straightforward. The author lays down a crucial rule: no proposition of the same type, nor any other type—except the general possible with opposite quantity and quality—can serve as the genuine contradictory. This lesson unpacks that rule and shows why other candidates fail, using the example of specific possibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original modal proposition
Take a modal proposition such as 'Every A is B with specific possibility' (e.g., 'Every human can write with difficulty'). Note its quantity (universal), quality (affirmative), and mode (specific possibility).
The author uses specific possibility as an example, but the rule applies to all modal propositions.
2
Understand the contradictory conditions
A true contradictory must be opposite in both quantity (universal vs. particular) and quality (affirmative vs. negative). Additionally, the two propositions can never be true together and can never be false together.
This is the standard condition for contradictories in Aristotelian logic.
3
Test candidates from the same mode
No proposition with the same mode (e.g., another specific possibility) can be a contradictory because they can both be false when the truth is a proposition with a different mode.
The author states: 'just as nothing of its species can contradict it'.
4
Test candidates from other modes
Other modal propositions, like the perpetual (da'ima) or the general absolute (mutlaqa 'amma), might seem like candidates but fail. For example, the general absolute opposite in quantity and quality can be false together with the original when the true proposition is 'Every A is B perpetually without necessity'.
The perpetual is a concomitant of the absolute necessary, so the general absolute is not a contradictory.
5
Confirm the only valid contradictory
The only proposition that always satisfies the conditions is the general possible (mumkina 'amma) that is opposite in quantity and quality. For 'Every A is B with specific possibility', the contradictory is 'Some A is not B with general possibility'.
The general possible expresses contingency and is the only mode that can contradict any modal proposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل «أب» بالإمكان الخاص. وكما أنه لا يمكن أن يناقضها من نوعها شيء فكذلك لا يمكن أن يناقضها غيرها سوى الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا. والعلم بذلك يفتقر إلى أن ينظر في كل قضية من القضايا الموجهة بعينها فإنه يظهر بالنظر فيها أنها من جملة ما لا يمكن أن يناقضها. وكيف يمكن وقد صح اجتماعهما على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق هو المخالف لهما في الجهة؛ وهذا هو الحكم الشامل لكل قضية من القضايا الموجهة. فما يوهم أن يناقضها سوى الممكنة العامة هو المطلقة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا لما أنها في مقابلة الدائمة. والدائمة من لوازم الضرورة المطلقة لكنه لا يكون كذلك فإنه يمكن اجتماعها على الكذب حال ما يكون الصادق قولنا كل «أب» دائمًا من غير ضرورة.
Every 'A is B' with specific possibility. And just as nothing of its species can contradict it, so too nothing other than the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality can contradict it. Knowledge of this requires examining each individual modal proposition, for it becomes clear upon examination that it is among those that cannot be contradicted. How can it, when it is confirmed that they (the original and the alleged contradictory) can both be false when the truth is the one that differs from them in mode? This is the comprehensive ruling for every modal proposition. What gives the illusion that something other than the general possible contradicts it is the general absolute that is opposite in quantity and quality, because it is in opposition to the perpetual. But the perpetual is a necessary concomitant of the absolute necessary, yet it is not like that, for they can both be false when the true statement is 'Every A is B perpetually without necessity'.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory (naqid) of modal propositions. The author begins with an example: a proposition with specific possibility (bi-l-imkan al-khass), e.g. 'Every A is B with specific possibility'. He states a general rule: just as no proposition of the same type (species) can contradict it, so too no other proposition can contradict it except the general possible (mumkina 'amma) that is opposite in both quantity (every vs. some not) and quality (affirmative vs. negative). This is because the original and the general possible can both be false when the true proposition is one that differs from both in mode. The author then addresses a potential confusion: someone might think that the general absolute (mutlaqa 'amma) opposite in quantity and quality is the contradictory, but this is false because the perpetual (da'ima) is a concomitant of the absolute necessary, and the general absolute can be false together with the original when the truth is a perpetual proposition without necessity. Thus the only true contradictory is the general possible.

Key Terms
الممكنة العامة
المخالفة كما وكيفا
الدائمة

Key Takeaway
The only contradictory of any modal proposition is the general possible proposition that is opposite in quantity and quality.

The Contradictory of the General Conditional from the Predicate Side
Author identifies the contradictory of the general conditional from the predicate side as the general possible opposite in quantity and quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and construct the contradictory of a general conditional proposition from the predicate side (e.g., 'Every A is B as long as it is B').

Core Idea
The contradictory lifts the predicate condition, flips quantity and quality, and becomes a possible proposition.

This lesson examines the contradictory of a specific type of conditional proposition: the general conditional from the predicate side (al-mashruta al-'amma min janib al-mahmul). These propositions have the form 'Every A is B as long as it is B' with necessity. The contradictory must deny this while removing the temporal restriction, resulting in a general possible proposition that is opposite in quantity (particular) and quality (negative). This rule is a cornerstone of immediate inference in Islamic logic, enabling precise refutation in theological and juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition's structure
The original is a general conditional from the predicate side: 'Every A is B as long as it is B' with necessity. Note the three restrictions: universality (every), affirmation (is B), and the temporal condition (as long as it is B).
The condition is attached to the predicate (B), not the subject.
2
Apply the contradictory rule
The contradictory must be the 'general possible' that is opposite in quantity (particular) and quality (negative), and it must lift the temporal condition from necessity to possibility. This yields 'Some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility'.
'General possible' here means a proposition that is possible and can be either universal or particular; the example uses particular.
3
Verify the result
Check that the contradictory is truly opposite: it denies the original by asserting that at least one A is not B at the very time it is B, but only possibly, not necessarily.
If the original were necessary, the contradictory cannot be necessary; it must be possible to avoid contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في المشروطة العامة من جانب المحمول فذلك وهو الذي يدل على رفع قيد من القيود هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» ما دام «ب»، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «ب» بالإمكان العام.
As for the general conditional from the predicate side, that which indicates the removal of a restriction is the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality, so it is said: necessarily, every A is B as long as it is B; some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of a general conditional proposition from the predicate side (mashruta 'amma min janib al-mahmul). This proposition has the form: 'Every A is B, as long as it is B' (with necessity). The contradictory here is similar to that of the subject side: the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality, but now the temporal condition is attached to the predicate. So the original is 'necessarily every A is B as long as it is B' and its contradictory is 'some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility'. The principle is the same: the contradictory must lift one of the three restrictions (here the predicate condition, quantity, and quality) and be possible.

Key Terms
المشروطة العامة من جانب المحمول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Some A is not B at all times

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a general conditional from the predicate side is the general possible proposition opposite in quantity and quality, which lifts the temporal condition from necessity to possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Immediate Inference
intermediate
5 min
Contradictory of Special Conditional from Predicate Side
Author gives two possible contradictories for the special conditional from the predicate side, analogous to the subject side.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible contradictories of a special conditional proposition from the predicate side, following the pattern from the subject side.

Core Idea
The special conditional's contradictory can be either a general possible opposite in quantity/quality or a perpetual absolute agreeing in quality.

In the previous lesson, you learned how to find the contradictory of a special conditional from the subject side. The author now extends that pattern to the predicate side. By understanding this analogy, you will be able to handle both types of special conditionals when performing immediate inferences in logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
Recognize the special conditional from the predicate side (al-mashruta al-khassa min janib al-mahmul). It includes the condition 'as long as it is B' and non-perpetuity, e.g., 'Every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is B'.
2
Recall the pattern from the subject side
The contradictory of the special conditional from the subject side had two possibilities: a general possible opposite in quantity and quality, or a perpetual absolute that agrees in quality.
This pattern is the foundation for the predicate side.
3
Apply the same pattern to the predicate side
The same two possibilities apply: (1) a general possible temporal opposite (e.g., 'some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility'), and (2) a perpetual absolute (e.g., 'some A is B perpetually').
The quantity and quality shift accordingly.
4
Verify with the given example
The passage explicitly states that the example mirrors the subject side: 'necessarily every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is B' yields the two contradictories listed.
This confirms the analogical extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المشروطة الخاصة من جانب المحمول فذلك هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» لا دائما بل ما دام (ب)، بعض (أ) ليس (ب) حين هو «ب» بالإمكان العام أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا على مثال ما مر من قبل في جانب الموضوع.
And in the special conditional from the predicate side, that is the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality, or the perpetual absolute that agrees in quality, so it is said: necessarily, every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is B; some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility; or some A is B perpetually, following the example that passed earlier on the subject side.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage treats the special conditional from the predicate side (mashruta khassa min janib al-mahmul). As with the subject side, it includes the extra restriction of non-perpetuity. The possible contradictories are again two: the general possible temporal opposite in quantity and quality, or the perpetual absolute that agrees in quality. The example mirrors the one given for the subject side: the original is 'necessarily every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is B' and the two candidates are 'some A is not B at the time when it is B with general possibility' and 'some A is B perpetually'. The author notes this follows the same pattern as before.

Key Terms
المشروطة الخاصة من جانب المحمول (al-mashruta al-khassa min janib al-mahmul): A special conditional proposition from the predicate side, including non-perpetuity, e.g. 'Every A is B as long as it is B, but not perpetually'. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a special conditional from the predicate side has two possible forms, exactly analogous to those from the subject side.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
